CITY OF SAN MATEO 
DRAFT ORDINANCE
An Ordinance Adding San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 2.22 and Amending Chapter 23.60 to update the 
Civic Arts Committee to be a Standing City Commission
WHEREAS, on March 3, 2025, the City Council directed staff to update San Mateo Municipal Code 
(“SMMC”) Chapter 23.60 to bring the Civic Arts Committee (“Committee”) into alignment with the appointment 
and term limits practices of other City advisory bodies; and
WHEREAS, the Committee was formed in 2008 as a special committee subject to the provisions of 
Section 6.09 of the San Mateo City Charter to support administration of the Art in Public Places Program; and
WHEREAS, the City Council has renewed the Civic Arts Committee every two years since its formation 
and now desires that it continue as a standing City commission; and
WHEREAS, the applicable sections of the Art in Public Places Ordinance (SMMC Chapter 23.60) are 
updated to reflect the title of the Civic Arts Commission.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. Chapter 2.22 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added to Title 2 as follows:
Chapter 2.22 
Civic Arts Commission
2.22.010 Organization.
The Civic Arts Commission of the City shall consist of no more than five members appointed by the 
Council, and two non-voting youth advisory members who must be at least 13 years old, and no more than 17 
years old at the time of appointment ("Youth Commissioners"). Youth Commissioners must present written 
documentation of parental or guardian consent to be considered for appointment. Youth commissioners shall 
serve only in an advisory capacity and shall not count towards a quorum of the commission. In making 
appointments, the Council shall prioritize appointing applicants who display an interest in and appreciation of 
art, architecture, local business, or the broader art community.
Each member of the Civic Arts Commission shall serve at the pleasure of the Council and for a term of 
four years or until the appointment of a successor, except that the initial terms of the first members appointed 
shall be determined by lot at their first meeting so that each year at least one term will expire. Thereafter, all 
appointments shall be for a term of four years. No member shall be eligible for reappointment after serving two 
consecutive four-year terms. Each Youth Commissioner shall serve at the pleasure of the Council for a term of 
one year and until the appointment and qualification of a successor. Youth Commissioners may be reappointed 
for one additional one-year term.
2.22.020 Meetings.
The Civic Arts Commission shall elect a chair and vice-chair to serve at the pleasure of the Commission.
A regular time and place of meetings shall be established and adhered to in the manner of holding public 
meetings for legislative bodies in the state. All meetings shall be open to the public unless otherwise provided by 
law.
88 of 551

--- page 89 ---
2.22.030 Powers – Duties.
It shall be the duty of the Civic Arts Commission, as an advisory body to the City Council, to advise on 
policies and programs related to public art as assigned and to carry out the duties as established in Chapter
23.60 (Art in Public Places).
Section 2. Section 23.60.020 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
23.60.020 Program Execution.
The Civic Arts Commission and the Community Development Department shall carry out the duties 
established by this chapter.
Section 3. Section 23.60.080 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
23.60.080 Approval for Placement of Artwork on Private Property
(a) Completed applications shall be submitted to the Community Development Department for review 
of the artwork.
(b) The Community Development Department shall present the completed application to the Civic Arts 
Commission. The Civic Arts Commission shall review the application for installation of the artwork considering its 
proposed location, the aesthetic quality and harmony with the proposed project, and the public accessibility to 
the artwork, including any recommended conditions of approval.
(c) The Civic Arts Commission shall approve a request to install artwork on private property, if it finds:
(1) The aesthetic quality of the artwork merits approval;
(2) The location of the proposed artwork is compatible and in harmony with the proposed 
development project and with the character of adjacent developed parcels; and
(3) There is sufficient public accessibility to the artwork.
(d) The decision of the Civic Arts Commission is subject to a fifteen-day review period by the City 
Council, and then becomes final. During this fifteen-day review period, any person may appeal a Civic Arts 
Commission decision to the City Council, who shall conduct a hearing thereon. The decision of the City Council 
shall be final.
Section 4. Section 23.60.100 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
23.60.100 Artwork on Public Property
(a) Every two years, the Civic Arts Commission shall prepare and submit to the City Council a report for 
the Art in Public Places Program. The report shall include a discussion of the amount of money in the Art in 
Public Places Fund ("the Fund"), any plans for the expenditure of money from the Fund, and any other matters 
the Civic Arts Commission deems appropriate to include in the report.
89 of 551

--- page 90 ---
90 of 551

--- page 91 ---
(b) Before money from the Fund is expended to purchase and install artwork on public property, the 
Civic Arts Commission shall consider the proposed expenditure and make a recommendation on the proposal to 
the City Council. In addition, at any time the Civic Arts Commission may make a recommendation to the City 
Council to purchase a particular artwork to be displayed on public property. Any recommendations made under 
this provision shall include the type of artwork considered, an analysis of the constraints applicable to placement 
of the artwork on a site, the need for and practicality of the maintenance of the artwork, and the costs of 
acquisition and installation of the artwork.

SUBJECT:
Human Resources and Finance Department Request for Additional Positions – Approval 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to add one (1) Full Time Equivalent (FTE) Human Resources Analyst position and one (1) FTE Payroll 
Technician I/II position.
BACKGROUND:
On July 28, 2025, the City Council approved an updated agreement between the City of San Mateo and the San Mateo 
Consolidated Fire Department (SMC Fire) for Finance and Human Resources services for a five (5)-year term from August 1, 
2025, through June 30, 2030. Among other revisions in the agreement, the City agreed to provide SMC Fire with one (1) 
FTE HR Analyst and one (1) FTE Payroll Technician I/II to support SMC Fire in Finance and Human Resources services. A 
third-party consultant conducted a study and recommended an additional two (2) FTE in staffing (for a total of 6 FTEs) to 
support the SMC Fire contract. These two new positions have since been added to the contract to reflect the service levels 
needed to meet contract expectations between the City and SMC Fire. In addition, the updated contract factors in the 
costs for these two positions. Based on the above, staff recommend the City Council authorize these two new positions. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The two positions are not currently in the FY 25-26 budget and will cost approximately $315,000 annually. However, staff 
does not recommend a new appropriation of funding as the current year cost will be a portion of this amount and the City 
will be receiving additional revenues from San Mateo Consolidated Fire Department to offset the cost. The full cost of the 
two positions will be included in the adopted budgets going forward. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not involve any 
commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)

All meeting noticing requirements were met.

STUDY SESSION
Citywide Facilities Condition Assessment – Informational
Steve Woo, Facilities & Fleet Services Manager, Matt Fabry, Public Works Director, and David Masenten, from 
ELS Architecture and Urban Design gave the presentation.
Public Comment: There were no speakers.
Council asked questions and made comments. Council provided direction to move forward using a blended 
strategy focused on Approach 2 (making like-for-like improvements to extend the useful life of priority facilities), 
Approach 3 (pursuing opportunities for strategic redevelopment at key sites), and Approach 4 (conducting 
citywide operational and programmatic assessments to guide future investments). Where necessary, the City 
will maintain the status quo and continue deferred maintenance (Approach 1), though the primary focus will be 
on forward-looking and strategic improvements. Staff and professional consultants will help determine which 
approach is most appropriate for each facility. Council emphasized the importance of equitable investment 
across all districts and committed to study sessions on key topics such as City Hall, recreation and aquatic 
facilities, and parking. This long-term planning effort is expected to unfold over the next 18–36 months, with 
regular five-year reviews as a standard practice of good governance.
ADJOURNMENT –The meeting adjourned at 6:48 p.m.

Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
Account Number: 26-3111
File ID: 25-10429
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
November 03, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Hillsdale Mall Redevelopment Application — Informational
RECOMMENDATION:
Receive an overview of the proposed project, receive public comments, and provide early feedback and direction to the 
applicant and staff.
BACKGROUND:
On February 6, 2025, the applicant submitted a preliminary application for a housing development project under the 
Housing Accountability Act (HAA) (Government Code Section 65941.1). Once deemed complete, an eligible housing 
development project vests in development standards, fees, and regulations as they existed at the time of submission, 
provided that all required documents outlined in the City’s SB 330 Preliminary Application Checklist are provided 
(https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/DocumentCenter/View/79071/Preliminary-Application-For-Housing-
Development?bidId=) . On March 20, 2025, with the submittal of all required information, the preliminary application was 
deemed complete. Following submittal of the preliminary application, both the applicant and the City sought clarification 
from the Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD) as to whether the project qualified as a “housing 
development project” pursuant to the HAA. As further discussed below, the HAA confers significant procedural and 
substantive protections to the project applicant, and the HAA must be interpreted and implemented to support housing 
development.
On August 12, 2025, HCD issued a technical assistance letter stating that the project qualified as a housing development 
project and was subject to the HAA (Attachment 1). The City then sought further clarification from HCD on the construction 
timing for residential components in this multi-phased mixed-use project. In a meeting on September 25, 2025, HCD staff 
verbally confirmed that jurisdictions may require the information listed in the City’s application submittal checklist to ensure 
that both the residential and commercial components are adequately planned. In other words, the City may require phasing 
information and add permitting requirements to support delivery of the residential components concurrently with the non-
residential components to ensure that the overall project continues to meet the criteria of a housing development project.
On June 20, 2025, the applicant submitted a formal planning application. The submission included a processing letter and 
consistency analysis, and a Master Development Plan set, both of which provided high-level information about the proposed 
project. However, the application did not include critical information, such as architectural design, building elevations, and 
detailed land uses and programs, even though these materials were required for the preliminary application to be deemed 
complete (Government Code Section 65941.1). On July 21, 2025, the City issued an incomplete letter based on the Planning 
Application Checklist for Non-Single-Family Projects (including SB330 applications). 
On October 17, 2025, the applicant resubmitted revised plans and application materials for the second round of review. 
Because this submission was received only a week and a half before agenda publication, this agenda report includes only 
101 of 551

--- page 102 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
high-level information from the second submittal. Staff from all reviewing departments are currently evaluating the updated 
application plans and documentation, with comments due by November 17, 2025. 
PROJECT SITE:
The project site consists of the main Hillsdale Shopping Center, bound by 31st Avenue to the north, El Camino Real to the 
east, Laurel Creek to the south, and Edison Street to the west, as well as a separate parcel consisting of a surface parking lot 
behind PetSmart Center on 36th Avenue, for a combined total of 32.66 acres. The shopping mall site and the surface parking 
lot are two separate parcels. The 12.03-acre North Block at Hillsdale Shopping Center, on the north side of 31st Avenue, is 
not part of the project site and will remain as currently developed. 
Proposed to be demolished as part of this project include the Hillsdale Shopping Center and associated parking structures, 
three commercial buildings that house Barnes & Noble, Trader Joe’s, and Wells Fargo/Citi Bank, as well as associated and 
standalone surface parking lots. Adjacent uses include a variety of commercial and residential uses:
•
North: Hillsdale North Block shopping mall
•
South: PetSmart and multi-family residential uses, separated from the project site by Laurel Creek
•
West: single-family uses 
•
East: Bay Meadow office development and single-family uses on the other side of El Camino Real and Railroad tracks.
In addition, the project site is located within ½-mile of major transit stops, which means that the project is exempt from all 
off-street parking requirements pursuant to AB 2097. The project site is also identified in the City’s 2023-2031 Housing 
Element as a housing opportunity site, with a potential capacity of 1,200 housing units. 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION:
The project proposes to demolish a significant portion of the Hillsdale Mall regional shopping center (approximately 1.5-
million square feet) and associated parking garage structures and subdivide the main mall site into 13 parcels through vesting 
tentative maps. The standalone surface parking lot at the south end of the project will remain as a separate parcel to be 
developed with residential uses. 
Conceptually, the main site is organized into four distinct land use zones: commercial zones along El Camino Real; a retail 
center in the northern portion of the site, providing a connection to the North Block; a residential zone along the western 
edge adjacent to Edison Street; and a flexible-use zone in the middle of site, bridging the commercial and residential areas.
To be specific, four newly created lots along El Camino Real are proposed to be office buildings ranging from five to ten 
stories, with potential ground-level retail spaces. The retail core is situated in two central blocks as standalone retail buildings 
and ground-level retail in two residential buildings. Residential development is concentrated on the western side, with five 
to eight-story apartment buildings in the mid-site area and a three to five-story apartment building and two rows of three 
to four-story townhomes along Edison Street as a transition zone to adjacent single-family residential neighborhood. The 
two central blocks between commercial and residential zones are programed as “flexible zones”, which may be developed 
with residential and/or commercial uses after the application approval. The Density Bonus Letter noted that the project 
would designate 14% of the total housing units for lower income (15% of the rental units for lower income household, and 
15% of the townhomes for moderate income).
The detailed land use information for each block was not included in the first-round submittal. A comparison of the overall 
land use programs between the preliminary application submittal and both formal application submittals is detailed in the 
table below.

DISCUSSION:
The Housing Accountability Act (HAA) sets processing deadlines and rigid review procedures for housing development 
projects. For example, the formal application is expected to be deemed complete within three cycles of review pursuant to 
Government Code section 65943. Otherwise, the City bears the burden to demonstrate that the incompleteness 
determination does not constitute an effective disapproval of the project. The HAA also prohibits jurisdictions from 
disapproving or conditionally approving a housing development project in a manner that renders the project infeasible, 
unless the project has a specific, adverse impact upon the public health and safety (Government Code Section 65589.5(d)). 
Equally important, the HAA only allows a jurisdiction to apply objective, quantifiable, written development standards, 
conditions, and policies in a manner to facilitate and accommodate development at the density permitted on the site and 
proposed by the development. 
Thus, the City Council’s discretionary authority is significantly limited regarding conditions and requirements that can be 
imposed on this project because of state housing laws regarding housing development projects.  In the past, the adoption 
of a Specific Plan or master development plan for a project of this size and scale would be a legislative action conducted 
through a discretionary review process, and potentially utilizing a development agreement, allowing the Planning 
Commission and City Council to set specific requirements and modifications based on the community and site-specific needs, 
and all applicable City plans, policies, and standards. 
Based on this context, staff has developed a list of high priority issues for the City Council to consider as part of this study 
session.
•
Issue 1 – Project Timeline and Phasing Plan
As currently submitted, the application does not include a timeline or phasing plan. In their original submittal, the 
applicant stated that the timeline is “not required in City published application checklist” and “specific phasing and 
sequence is expected to vary based on market conditions at the time of redevelopment to ensure Project 
financeability.” Based on the applicant’s Hillsdale Reimagined Website, the complete redevelopment is estimated 
to occur in phases over the next 20 years, which is also referenced in the applicant-held neighborhood meeting on 
April 29, 2025. 
Staff are actively working with the applicant and consulting with HCD to ensure that the project is processed and 
constructed in compliance with the state law and local regulations. Absence of phasing and timeline information 
1 Up to 1,670 units identified on Master Plan Document
2 Up to 2,390,800 sq.ft. identified on Master Plan Document
3 Up to 2,059,000 sq.ft. identified on Master Plan Document
103 of 551

--- page 104 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
adds uncertainty given the project’s complexity and extended duration. Key technical studies, such as utility capacity 
analysis, water supply assessment, and traffic analysis, also depend on the project’s phasing plan. 
As a housing development project, the application is subject to a tight timeline and limited to three rounds of review 
to determine application completeness with City requirements. Each of these review cycles starts with a 30-day City 
review, followed by a 90-day period for the applicant to respond to City comments. Based on three rounds of review, 
the project’s completeness review would finish in March 2026. 
Crucially, the phasing of residential development remains unclear, and City staff are continuing to work with the 
applicant to help support delivery of residential components concurrently and proportionately with non-
residential components consistent with the City’s BMR guidelines.  As stated above, this is to ensure that the overall 
project delivers housing units as the commercial components are built.
After review for completeness, the City must provide written documentation identifying any inconsistencies with 
local regulations within 60 days of being deemed complete (Government Code Section 65589.5(j)(2)(A)(ii)). A list of 
policies and codes in the City’s General Plan, adopted plans and the Zoning Code that may be applicable to the 
project is included as Attachment 4. The applicant is expected to address all the inconsistency issues while the 
environmental (CEQA) analysis prepared. Following completion of the environmental review, the City must schedule 
public hearings to consider approval of the project. 
•
Issue  2 – Regional Shopping Center Designation and Community Serving Commercial
The Hillsdale Station Area Plan (HSAP) identifies the Hillsdale Mall as a regional retail and employment center, while 
also recognizing its potential for housing development opportunities (Policy LU-2.4). The HSAP anticipates that any 
major modification to the mall or surrounding properties would require preparation of a comprehensive master 
plan. When the HSAP was adopted, such a master plan was typically processed through discretionary review and 
adopted as a legislative action. However, this process is no longer applicable to a housing development project, 
unless the applicant voluntarily engages with the City in a conversation to preserve the regional retail function 
consistent with the Area Plan’s vision.
The proposed demolition of approximately 1.5 million square feet of existing retail and commercial space, along 
with associated parking, and its replacement with only ground-level retail space would represent a significant loss 
of regional commercial activity. Approval of the Hillsdale Mall Redevelopment project as currently proposed would 
leave the City with BridgePoint as the sole remaining regional retail center. However, the redevelopment of the site 
and added office uses will support increased property tax revenue and local jobs. To fully assess these issues, the 
City will be engaging an economic consultant and retail consultant to provide a comprehensive evaluation of the 
proposed project, including how it will impact the local economy and City revenues. 
Furthermore, the project proposes to develop “up to” 1,670 new housing units (or 1,389 units as identified on the 
last submitted Plan Set ) which will generate substantial demand for community-serving retail and commercial 
services. For comparison, Bay Meadows Phase I included 734 residential units and 300,000 square feet of 
retail/commercial space, and Phase II included 1,048 homes and 150,000 square feet of retail/commercial space. 
Although the applicant introduces a grocery store in Building E1 as part of the second-round submittal, the total 
amount and type of proposed retail/commercial space is still undefined. To help meet the needs of both existing 
and new residents, it would be ideal for the project to include sufficient space for retail and commercial service 
businesses to serve local needs and continue to be a regional destination.
•
Issue 3 – Pedestrian Connection to Hillsdale Caltrain Station
Since the project is exempt from parking requirements under state law, a strong connection to the Hillsdale Caltrain 
Station and transit along El Camino Real is critical to maximize transit use and support the viability of reduced off-
street parking. Implementing a pedestrian bridge linking the station and the mall across El Camino Real would not 
only enhance connectivity but also improve pedestrian safety, encourage transit-oriented development, and 
strengthen the overall vitality of the site.
104 of 551

--- page 105 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
•
Issue 4 – Off-Street Parking
The project proposes extensive ground-level parking for both residential and commercial buildings, rather than 
maximizing ground-level retail space, which could result in a suboptimal pedestrian experience along El Camino Real 
and the newly created internal streets. A standalone parking structure (Building C5) is also proposed in the center 
of this site. Because the project is located within one-half mile of Hillsdale Caltrain Station, the City cannot impose 
any parking requirements pursuant to AB 2097. The applicant, however, may voluntarily work with the City to locate 
parking strategically to maximize both the feasibility and vitality of the project.
•
Issue 5 – Traffic and Circulation
Under SB 743 (Public Resources Code Section 21099), if a project is located within one-half mile of a major transit 
stop, the project may be presumed to have a less-than-significant Vehicle Mile Traveled (VMT) impact, especially for 
residential and office uses, unless substantial evidence shows otherwise. In other words, projects near transit can 
streamline traffic analysis under CEQA. However, General Plan 2040’s Circulation Element, specifically policies C 6.3 
and C 6.4, require site-specific transportation impact analysis following the City’s adopted Transportation Impact 
Analysis (TIA) Policy for development projects. City staff is currently working with its consultant team to prepare a 
transportation impact analysis (TIA) to evaluate the project and what improvements will be needed to minimize any 
potential impacts.
•
Issue 6 – Site and Architectural Design Standards
The architectural design, submitted in the second-round submittal, is under staff review to evaluate its consistency 
with San Mateo’s Objective Design Standards. At a high level, staff will focus on the overall design quality of the 
tallest office buildings fronting along El Camino Real, the compatibility of the proposed residential buildings with the 
surrounding neighborhood, and the quality of ground-level interfaces with the public realm.
•
Issue 7 – Environmental Review
The applicant is seeking a CEQA exemption pursuant to Section 15183, which would allow the project to tier off of 
a previously certified program-level Environmental Impact Report (EIR) when the project is consistent with the 
underlying general plan and its policies. In this case, the applicant proposes to tier from the General Plan 2040 EIR, 
arguing that the Hillsdale Mall Redevelopment project falls within the scope of the General Plan’s land use and 
development policies, thereby streamlining the environmental review process. However, if there are any site-
specific impacts that require further study, the project would not be eligible for this exemption. For the proposed 
project, factors such as (but not limited to) water supply, utility capacity, construction traffic, noise and vibration, 
air quality, and proximity to Laurel Creek could indicate potential site-specific significant effects, which would 
require preparation of an initial study and/or EIR. The project, however, is exempt from VMT analysis and aesthetic 
impact review under SB 743, as it is located within one-half mile of a major transit stop. 
Staff is seeking input from the City Council on the project, including but not limited to the discussion topics outlined above. 
Early feedback from the Council and the public will help inform the next steps of the application process to the extent 
possible and will assist the applicant in further updating and refining the design of the proposed project.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This study session is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical 
change in the environment (Public Resources Code Section 21065). The level of environmental review required for this 
project is still being assessed.

Dear Sung Kwon: 
 
RE: City of San Mateo – 60 E 31st Avenue – Letter of Technical Assistance 
 
The California Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD) received a 
request from the applicant of the proposed project at 60 E 31st Avenue (Project) 
regarding qualification as a housing development project under the Housing 
Accountability Act (HAA). Additionally, City of San Mateo (City) staff requested 
assistance with construction deadlines and the potential for expanding the number of 
review periods under the HAA and the Permit Streamlining Act (PSA). 
 
Background 
 
The Project is proposed on the site of the existing Hillsdale Mall. The Project proposes 
to demolish approximately 1.5 million square feet of commercial space and to construct 
2 million square feet of commercial space and 569,000 square feet of residential area. 
The residential portion will be comprised of 1,392 units, including 209 units restricted to 
low-income households.  
 
The Project applicant submitted a preliminary application on February 5, 2025. The City 
provided a letter determining that the preliminary application was incomplete on March 
7, 2025, with the applicant responding to the incomplete letter on March 20, 2025. The 
City provided a follow-up clarification letter on March 28, 2025, primarily citing concerns 
about the Project’s eligibility as a housing development project under the HAA.  
 
 
 
107 of 551

--- page 108 ---
Sung Kwon, Deputy Director of Community Development 
Page 2 
 
 
 
Question: What qualifies as a “housing development project” under Government 
Code section 65589.5, subdivision (h)(2)(B)(iii)? 
 
To qualify for protections under the HAA, a project must meet the definition of a 
“housing development project.” The HAA provides several avenues to meet this 
definition.1 The Project is specifically seeking to meet the criteria under Government 
Code section 65589.5, subdivision (h)(2)(B)(iii), under which “[a]t least 50 percent of the 
net new or converted square footage is designated for residential use” and the Project 
meets additional criteria. 
 
HCD finds that the Project meets the 50 percent residential minimum as proposed. The 
statute specifically states “net new” when discussing square footage of construction. 
The net new square footage for the Project is calculated by subtracting the existing 
square footage from the total proposed new square footage, which gives 1.07 million 
square feet. Because the residential portion of the Project is 569,000 square feet, 
approximately 53 percent of the net new square footage is residential. 
 
Under Government Code section 65589.5, subdivision (h)(2)(B)(iii), the Project must 
also contain at least 500 net new residential units, involve the demolition or conversion 
of at least 100,000 square feet of nonresidential space, demolish at least 50 percent of 
existing nonresidential uses, and must not contain transient lodging. The Project meets 
these thresholds by proposing to develop 1,392 new residential units and to demolish all 
1.5 million square feet of existing nonresidential space and replace it with 2 million 
square feet of commercial space and 569,000 square feet of residential space. The 
Project does not include transient lodging. Therefore, HCD finds that all these criteria, 
plus the 50 percent residential minimum, are met. Thus, the Project qualifies as a 
housing development project under the HAA.  
 
Question: Does the entire project remain vested once construction begins on a 
single building—potentially a commercial-only building—or must construction 
commence on all buildings (including residential) within the 2.5-year period? 
 
The HAA states that the application will lose vesting of the preliminary application under 
Government Code section 65941.1 if the housing development project has not 
commenced construction within 2.5 years, or 3.5 years for an affordable housing 
project, following the date that the project receives final approval.2 Statute does not 
specify the types or ratios of construction that must be commenced. Therefore, a 
commercial-only building that is part of an overall proposed project would satisfy the 
construction deadline for the purpose of maintaining vesting. In other words, the entire 
proposal is considered a “housing development project,” including the commercial 
component, and starting construction on any aspect (residential or nonresidential) 
maintains vesting.  
 
1 Gov. Code, § 65589.5, subd. (h)(2). 
2 Gov. Code, § 65589.5, subd. (o)(2)(D). 
108 of 551

--- page 109 ---
Sung Kwon, Deputy Director of Community Development 
Page 3 
 
 
 
 
Question: Can a jurisdiction extend the number of incompleteness 
determinations under the PSA? 
 
The HAA requires that applications for housing development projects be deemed 
complete within the timeframes stated in Government Code section 65943, also known 
as the Permit Streamlining Act (PSA).3 If after two resubmittals of the application, the 
City finds the application is incomplete, the City bears the burden of showing the finding 
of incompleteness is not an effective disapproval of the project. The City may not extend 
the number of incompleteness determinations without justification from the City or if the 
applicant agrees to extend the number of determinations voluntarily. The HAA and PSA 
are intended to streamline the application process, and additional review cycles would 
be contrary to that intent. 
 
Conclusion 
 
HCD finds that the Project qualifies as a housing development project under the HAA 
and urges City staff to process the application accordingly. Additionally, it should be 
noted that construction deadlines under the HAA may be satisfied with commencement 
of any part of the Project (residential or nonresidential), and the number of review 
periods may only be extended if either the applicant voluntarily agrees or the City can 
provide justification for remaining incomplete items. 
 
If you have any questions regarding the content of this letter or would like additional 
technical assistance, please contact Bentley Regehr at bentley.regehr@hcd.ca.gov.

the City’s recent Incompleteness Letter comments. 
 
Since our last submission, our team has made a concerted effort to respond fully and thoughtfully 
to each of the City’s comments. In every instance, even where a comment extended beyond the 
explicit requirements of the submission checklist, we have sought to provide information that 
directly addresses the City’s feedback and advances our shared goal of a thorough, transparent, 
and collaborative review process. 
 
This resubmittal addresses all of the City’s comments in order to achieve “completeness” under 
SB330, and we look forward to moving the planning process forward with City staff 
collaboratively.  We also recognize and appreciate that the totality of the information contained in 
this re-submittal is substantial and that the resources and effort required of staff to process this 
application is significant. To that end, we are eager to continue working closely with staff to ensure 
that each element is well understood and properly documented, and we will make ourselves 
available to meet  as frequently as the City finds helpful during its follow-up review. 
 
Summary of Key Updates 
In addition to fully addressing the City’s comments, this submittal further develops and refines 
several substantive aspects of the Project: 
 
• Open Space/Public Realm: The distinct identities and designs of the various open spaces 
within the project have been further developed – from the grassy expanse of Hillsdale 
Square to the planter-lined greenway of the Neighborhood Passage. Taken together, the 
site plan weaves together a diverse and extensive open space network that provides a 
variety of uses and activities that will not only activate the property throughout the day and

• Building Architecture: Although we believe the architectural form of each building will 
continue to evolve significantly after completeness and then furthermore during subsequent 
SPAR applications, this resubmittal package includes elevations and architecture for each 
building so that the community has more information about what the project could look 
like upon completion.  
 
• Retail and Ground Plane: Throughout the design and engagement process, we have 
emphasized that the ground plane is the most important element of the project, as this is 
the space through which the majority of visitors, shoppers, residents, and workers will 
experience. Although the 20th-century version of mall retailing is disappearing, 
appropriately sized, vibrant, and activated retail districts such as those proposed for 
Hillsdale are thriving. The updated plans demonstrate how a series of two-sided streets and 
plazas, accommodate uses that are “outward facing” and engage with the activated public 
open space, that come together to create a larger overall district.  Additionally, a large-
format grocer has been programmed into the ground level of the E1 building at the corner 
of El Camino and 31st avenue, reflecting both the feedback and desires that we have heard 
from the community, as well as reflecting the flexibility of the building footprints and their 
ability to accommodate a myriad of uses.  
 
• Illustrative Renderings: Finally, we have included illustrative photorealistic renderings 
within the updated submission to better convey how one would feel experiencing different 
parts of the redeveloped property.  While these images provide a clearer sense of place and 
design intent, we understand and expect that the architecture will continue to evolve, and 
these photorealistic renderings are intended to convey the general intent, with respect to 
scale, quality, organization, and use. They purposely do not directly correspond with the 
architectural elevations in the remaining portions of the Application Checklist Plan set, as 
these renderings are intended to be a launching point for ongoing architectural discussion 
and refinement after completeness. 
 
We understand that project refinement is an iterative process. While this resubmission represents 
a significant advancement and a complete response to the City’s comments, we fully expect—and 
welcome—additional collaboration and refinement after the City deems the application complete. 
Our team looks forward to ongoing dialogue to ensure the Project continues to evolve in a way 
that reflects both the City’s objectives and the community’s aspirations.

• Grocery Store Programming: As described above, a grocery store has been incorporated

Autodesk Docs://23.04025.00 - Hillsdale MP Peer Review/HILLSDALE-HOK-AR.rvt
PROJECT
INFORMATION
23.04025.00
2025
G003
PROJECT DESCRIPTION
THIS PLAN SET SUPPLEMENTS THE HILLSDALE RE-IMAGINED MASTER DEVELOPMENT PLAN (MDP) AND RESPONDS TO 
THE CITY OF SAN MATEO’S JULY 21, 2025 INCOMPLETE LETTER FOR PLANNING APPLICATION PA-2025-052. IT 
PROVIDES DETAILED DIAGRAMS, TECHNICAL DRAWINGS, AND SUPPORTING DOCUMENTATION TO DEMONSTRATE 
CONSISTENCY WITH THE MDP VISION AND COMPLIANCE WITH APPLICABLE PLANNING REQUIREMENTS.
THE HILLSDALE RE-IMAGINED PROJECT PROPOSES THE PHASED REDEVELOPMENT OF APPROXIMATELY 32.66 ACRES 
WITHIN THE HILLSDALE SHOPPING CENTER, TRANSFORMING THE SITE INTO A VIBRANT, MIXED-USE DISTRICT. THE 
PLAN REPLACES EXISTING MALL AND BIG-BOX RETAIL STRUCTURES WITH A WALKABLE NEIGHBORHOOD THAT 
INTEGRATES:
• 
UP TO 1,670 NEW RESIDENTIAL UNITS, INCLUDING APPROXIMATELY 200 BELOW-MARKET-RATE (BMR)
HOMES.
• 
UP TO 570,000 SQUARE FEET OF NET NEW COMMERCIAL SPACE, INCLUDING RETAIL, OFFICE, AND 
RESEARCH USES.
• 
AN INTERCONNECTED 4.5-ACRE OPEN SPACE NETWORK, FEATURING PLAZAS, GREENWAYS, AND PARKLETS.
THIS PLAN SET ILLUSTRATES THE PROPOSED SITE LAYOUT, BUILDING FOOTPRINTS, PARKING AND CIRCULATION 
SYSTEMS, UTILITY INFRASTRUCTURE, GRADING AND DRAINAGE, AND LANDSCAPE DESIGN. IT ALSO INCLUDES 
UPDATED SQUARE FOOTAGE TABLES, DENSITY CALCULATIONS, AND BLOCK-LEVEL USE SUMMARIES TO CLARIFY 
COMPLIANCE WITH GOVERNMENT CODE SECTION 65589.5(H)(2)(B)(III), CONFIRMING THE PROJECT QUALIFIES AS A 
HOUSING DEVELOPMENT UNDER THE HOUSING ACCOUNTABILITY ACT.
THE MATERIALS HEREIN ADDRESS COMPLETENESS ITEMS OUTLINED IN THE CITY’S LETTER, INCLUDING:
• 
CLARIFICATION OF RESIDENTIAL AND COMMERCIAL SQUARE FOOTAGES.
• 
DEMONSTRATION OF MINIMUM AND MAXIMUM DENSITIES PER BLOCK.
• 
UPDATED PLOT PLANS, LIGHTING AND SIGNAGE DIAGRAMS, AND UTILITY CONNECTION POINTS.
• 
DRAFT COVENANTS, TENTATIVE MAP DETAILS, AND ARBORIST DOCUMENTATION.
PREPARED BY A QUALIFIED DESIGN TEAM INCLUDING LICENSED ARCHITECTS, LANDSCAPE ARCHITECTS, CIVIL 
ENGINEERS, AND LAND PLANNERS, THIS PLAN SET IS INTENDED TO SUPPORT THE CITY’S REVIEW AND FACILITATE 
THE NEXT PHASE OF ENTITLEMENT PROCESSING.

BUILDING
UNSHADED SITE
SHADED SITE
At 9:00 AM on March 21st, the shadow study was performed, with 
the corresponding solar path and sun altitude clearly indicated in the 
diagrams. 
During this period, portions of the pedestrian walkways and some edges 
of the public spaces are shaded by adjacent building masses. While this 
results in limited direct sunlight in the early morning, such conditions are 
typical in urban environments.

L400
HYDROZONE NOTES
AND SCHEDULE
IRRIGATION NOTES
IRRIGATION MAINTENANCE SCHEDULE
1.
THE SYSTEM HAS BEEN DESIGNED TO PROVIDE 100% COVERAGE. ANY CHANGES MADE IN THE LAYOUT DUE TO FIELD
CONDITIONS SHALL BE IN ACCORDANCE WITH THESE STANDARDS. QUANTITIES IN SCHEDULE ARE ESTIMATED. PLAN
SHALL TAKE PRECEDENCE.
2.
ALL IRRIGATION LINES AND VALVES ARE SHOWN DIAGRAMMATICALLY. ALL LINES AND VALVES TO BE INSTALLED IN
PLANTING AREAS WHERE POSSIBLE.
3.
CONTRACTOR TO FIELD LOCATE ALL PROPOSED IRRIGATION WATER MAIN LINE LOCATIONS. CONTACT LANDSCAPE
ARCHITECT PRIOR TO START OF WORK IF DISCREPANCIES BETWEEN THIS PLAN AND EXISTING CONDITIONS ARE FOUND.
4.
LOCATE ALL VALVES INSIDE LANDSCAPE AREAS, ALLOWING ACCESS FOR MAINTENANCE PURPOSES, BUT HIDING THEM
FROM PUBLIC VIEW WHENEVER POSSIBLE.
5.
ALL PRESSURE MAINLINES UNDER ASPHALT PAVEMENT SHALL BE PLACED WITHIN SLEEVES AS NOTED. WHERE ELECTRIC
VALVE CONTROL LINES PASS THROUGH A SLEEVE WITH OTHER MAIN OR LATERAL LINES THEY SHALL BE CONTAINED
WITHIN A SEPARATE, SMALLER CONDUIT.
6.
CONTRACTOR SHALL PROVIDE "AS-BUILT" DRAWINGS OF THE FINAL INSTALLATION TO OWNER AT SUBSTANTIAL
COMPLETION BEFORE RECEIVING FINAL PAYMENT.
7.
ALL SLEEVES UTILIZED BY THE IRRIGATION CONTRACTOR, WHETHER INSTALLED BY HIM OR NOT, SHALL BE LOCATED ON
THE "AS-BUILT" DRAWINGS. THE DEPTH BELOW FINISH GRADE,  TO THE NEAREST FOOT OF EACH END OF EACH SLEEVE
SHALL BE NOTED AT EACH SLEEVE LOCATION ON THE "AS-BUILT"  DRAWINGS. ALL SLEEVES SHALL BE SIZED TWO PIPE
SIZES GREATER THAN PIPE IT CARRIES.
8.
IRRIGATION CONTRACTOR SHALL SECURE ANY AND ALL NECESSARY PERMITS FOR THE WORK PRIOR TO COMMENCEMENT
OF HIS OPERATIONS ON-SITE. COPIES OF THE PERMITS SHALL BE  SENT TO THE OWNER/GENERAL CONTRACTOR. WORK IN
THE  R.O.W. SHALL CONFORM TO THE STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS OF LOCAL AND/OR STATE HIGHWAY
JURISDICTION.
9.
VERIFY CONTROLLER AND RAIN SENSOR LOCATION AND MAINLINE POINT OF CONNECTION AT PROJECT SITE WITH OWNER.
10. ELECTRIC SERVICE TO CONTROLLER SHALL BE PROVIDED BY THE GENERAL CONTRACTOR.
11. INSTALLATION OF WORK SHALL BE COORDINATED WITH OTHER  CONTRACTORS IN SUCH A MANNER AS TO ALLOW FOR A
SPEEDY  AND ORDERLY COMPLETION OF ALL WORK ON THE SITE.
12.
COORDINATE WITH PLANTING PLAN FOR PLANTER BED LOCATIONS AND TREE LOCATIONS.
13. PRIOR TO THE START OF CONSTRUCTION, CONTRACTOR SHALL COORDINATE WITH DEVELOPER FOR OPERATING
PARAMETERS OF MASTER SYSTEM.  THIS DESIGN REQUIRES STATIC 83 PSI TO OPERATE.  IF THE MASTER SYSTEM CANNOT
PROVIDE THESE PARAMETERS, CONTRACTOR SHALL MAKE ADJUSTMENTS TO THE DESIGN BY ADDING CONTROL VALVES,
A BOOSTER PUMP, PRESSURE REDUCING VALVE, OR OTHER EQUIPMENT, AS NECESSARY.  CONTRACTOR SHALL SUBMIT
DESIGN REVISIONS TO OWNER'S REPRESENTATIVE FOR APPROVAL PRIOR TO SUBMITTING BID.
14.
A FINAL REPORT FOR THE TESTING AND ADJUSTING OF ALL NEW SYSTEMS SHALL BE COMPLETED PRIOR TO FINAL
APPROVAL BY THE FIELD INSPECTOR. THIS REPORT SHALL BE SIGNED BY THE INDIVIDUAL RESPONSIBLE FOR
PERFORMING THESES SERVICES.
15.
A LAMINATED DIAGRAM OF THE IRRIGATION PLAN SHOWING HYDROZONES SHALL BE KEPT WITH THE IRRIGATION
CONTROLLER FOR SUBSEQUENT MANAGEMENT PURPOSES.
16.
A CERTIFICATE OF COMPLETION SHALL BE FILLED OUT AND CERTIFIED BY EITHER THE SIGNER OF THE LANDSCAPE PLANS,
THE SIGNER OF THE IRRIGATION PLANS, OR THE LICENSED LANDSCAPE CONTRACTOR FOR THE PROJECT.
17.
AN IRRIGATION AUDIT REPORT SHALL BE COMPLETED AT THE TIME OF FINAL INSPECTION.
18.
ALL INSTALLED IRRIGATION LINES MUST MAINTAIN A 3'-0" HORIZONTAL CLEARANCE AND 1'-0" VERTICAL CLEARANCE FROM
ALL JOINT TRENCH DRY UTILITIES, ROUTING AND EQUIPMENT. (3'-0" HORIZONTAL CLEARANCE MEASURED FROM EDGE TO
EDGE OF PIPES.)
THE IRRIGATION MAINTENANCE SCHEDULE TASKS LISTED BELOW ARE INTENDED AS MINIMUM STANDARDS AND MORE
FREQUENT ATTENTION MAY BE REQUIRED DEPENDING ON THE PARTICULAR SITE CONDITIONS. MAINTENANCE SHALL BE DONE
TO ENSURE WATER EFFICIENCY. REPAIR OF IRRIGATION EQUIPMENT SHALL BE DONE WITH THE ORIGINALLY SPECIFIED
MATERIALS OR APPROVED EQUIVALENTS.
FREQUENCY - QUARTERLY
TASK - CONTROLLER CABINET : OPEN CABINET AND CLEAN OUT DEBRIS AND REPLACE BATTERY AS NECESSARY.CHECK
WIRING AND REPAIR AS NEEDED AND CHECK CLOCK AND RESET IF NECESSARY.
FREQUENCY - MONTHLY
TASK - IRRIGATION SCHEDULE: ADJUST SCHEDULE FOR SEASONAL VARIATIONS AND OTHER CONDITIONS WHICH MAY AFFECT
THE AMOUNT OF WATER NEEDED TO MAINTAIN PLANT HEALTH. ADJUST AS NECESSARY.
FREQUENCY - QUARTERLY
TASK - POC: VISUALLY INSPECT COMPONENTS FOR LEAKS, PRESSURE SETTINGS, SETTLEMENT OR OTHER DAMAGE
AFFECTING THE OPERATION OF A COMPONENT. REPAIR AS NEEDED.
FREQUENCY - QUARTERLY
TASK - REMOTE CONTROL VALVES : ISOLATION VALVES AND QUICK COUPLER VALVES: VISUALLY INSPECT FOR LEAKS,
SETTLEMENTS, WIRE CONNECTIONS AND PRESSURE SETTINGS. REPAIR AS NEEDED.
FREQUENCY - QUARTERLY
TASK - MAINLINE AND LATERALS: VISUALLY INSPECT FOR LEAKS OR SETTLEMENTS OF TRENCH.
FREQUENCY - WEEKLY
TASK -  FILTERS AND STRAINERS - VISUALLY CHECK FOR ANY BROKEN MALIGNED OR CLOGGED HEADS, 
HEADS 
WITH
INCORRECT ARC, INADEQUATE COVERAGE OR OVERSPRAY AND LOW HEAD DRAINAGE. REPAIR AS NEEDED.
FREQUENCY - MONTHLY
TASK - FILTERS AND STRAINERS: VISUALLY CHECK FOR LEAKS, BROKEN FITTINGS. CLEAN AND FLUSH SCREENS.
I HAVE COMPLIED WITH THE CRITERIA OF THE WATER EFFICIENT LANDSCAPE ORDINANCE AND APPLIED THEM FOR THE
EFFICIENT USE OF WATER IN THE IRRIGATION DESIGN PLAN.
NICOLE KELLY, LLA 6011
DECODERS
CONTROLLER SHALL INTERFACE WITH HUNTER ICD DECODERS, EACH CAPABLE OF CONTROLLING 1, 2, 4, OR 6 VALVES (ICD-100,
ICD-200, ICD-400, AND ICD-600)
PROVIDE AN ICD-SEN SENSOR DECODER FOR FLOW SENSOR(S) AND/OR CLIK SENSOR(S) ON TWO WIRE PATH
WIRE CONNECTIONS FROM DECODER OUTPUT TO SOLENOID SHALL BE 14 AWG, TYPE PE
WIRE DISTANCE FROM DECODER OUTPUT TO SOLENOID UNDER NORMAL CONDITIONS SHALL NOT EXCEED 150-FT [45-M]
INSTALL IN VALVE BOX ON DECODER STAKE KIT (DECSTAKE-10) WITH BOTTOM OF DECODER FACING UP
CONTRACTOR SHALL INDICATE ASSOCIATED VALVE NUMBER(S) ON MANUFACTURER PROVIDED LABEL ON DECODER WITH
PERMANENT MARKER
WIRE
WIRE FOR TWO-WIRE PATH SHALL BE TWISTED AND JACKETED HUNTER IDWIRE, OR APPROVED EQUAL (PAIGE ELECTRIC
P7354D); COATED WIRE SHALL NOT BE ACCEPTED AS AN EQUAL. ACCEPTABLE EQUAL PRODUCTS MUST CONSIST OF TWO
SEPARATELY PE JACKETED WIRE TWISTED INSIDE OF A PE JACKET
CONTRACTOR SHALL INSTALL IDWIRE1 (14 AWG) FOR WIRE PATH LENGTH UP TO 10,000-FT [3,048-M] AND IDWIRE2 (12 AWG) FOR
WIRE PATH LENGTH UP TO 15,000-FT [4,572-M], WIRE PATH LENGHTS DECREASE WITH SUBSTITUTED WIRE
WIRE JACKET COLORS SHALL BE SUCH TO FACILITATE THE IDENTIFICATION OF VARIOUS WIRE PATH ZONES; SEE WIRE JACKET
CHART FOR WIRE TYPE, COLOR AND ASSOCIATED VALVES
THE CONTROLLER ALLOWS UP TO THREE (3) TWO-WIRE PATHS PER OUTPUT MODULE, CONTRACTOR SHALL NOT CONNECT
ANY TWO-WIRE PATH FROM ONE OUTPUT MODULE TO ANOTHER OUTPUT MODULE
WIRE CONNECTION FROM DECODER OUTPUT TO SOLENOID SHALL BE COLORED TO MATCH THE ASSOCIATED DECODER
OUTPUT STATION COLOR; RED AND BLUE COLORED WIRES SHALL NOT BE USED FOR CONNECTION BETWEEN DECODER
OUTPUT AND SOLENOID
SPLICES
ALL CONNECTIONS AND SPLICES IN THE RED/BLUE TWO-WIRE PATH MUST BE MADE WITH 3M DBR/Y-6 WATERPROOF
CONNECTORS INSTALLED PER MANUFACTURERS INSTRUCTIONS IN VALVE BOX WITH OPEN END OF CONNECTOR FACING
DOWN
CONTRACTOR SHALL PROVIDE 36-IN [1-M] LOOP OF SLACK WIRE, MEASURED FROM TOP OF VALVE BOX, NEATLY COILED INSIDE
ALL SPLICE BOXES AND VALVE BOXES
ANY SPLICES IN THE TWO-WIRE PATH NOT ASSOCIATED WITH A DECODER SHALL BE HOUSED IN SEPARATE VALVE BOXES WITH
36-IN [1-M] LOOP OF SLACK WIRE
CONTRACTOR SHALL INDICATE TWO-WIRE PATH DIRECTIONS IN PERMANENT MARKER WITHIN 6-IN [2.5-CM] OF TWO-WIRE
SPLICE ON WIRE JACKET OR ID TAG ZIP TIED TO WIRE:
INCOMING WIRE SHALL BE MARKED “CONTROLLER” ON WIRE JACKET OR ID TAG AND MUST INCLUDE ZIP-TIE ATTACHED TO
WIRE JACKET
EACH OUTGOING TWO-WIRE PATH SHALL BE MARKED WITH CONNECTED VALVES ON WIRE JACKET
CONTRACTOR SHALL ENSURE ALL CONNECTIONS TO BE WATERTIGHT WITH NO ELECTRICAL LEAKAGE TO GROUND OR
SHORTING BETWEEN CONDUCTORS
GROUNDING
ALL GROUNDING AND INSTALLATION OF EQUIPMENT SPECIFIED SHALL BE INSTALLED IN STRICT COMPLIANCE WITH THE
MANUFACTURER’S RECOMMENDATIONS AND IN ACCORDANCE WITH LOCAL, STATE, AND FEDERAL REQUIREMENTS
BOTH THE CONTROLLER AND THE DECODERS SHALL BE GROUNDED TO GROUND RODS OR PLATES WITH LESS THAN 10 OHMS
RESISTANCE
IRRIGATION CONTROLLER AND PAD SHALL NOT FALL WITHIN THE SPHERE OF INFLEUNCE OF A GROUND ROD OR PLATE
AT A MINIMUM, EARTH GROUND SHALL BE CONNECTED AT THE FIRST DECODER OF EACH WIRE PATH LEAVING THE
CONTROLLER, AND EVERY 12TH VALVE/DECODER OR 1,000-FT [304-M] OF TWO-WIRE RUN (WHICHEVER IS SHORTER), AND AT
THE LAST VALVE/DECODER IN ANY WIRE RUN EXCEEDING 50’ FROM MAIN WIRE PATH
FOR USE OF GROUNDING PLATE:
SOLID COPPER GROUNDING PLATE SHALL HAVE A PRE-WELDED #6 AWG INSULATED GREEN-YELLOW WIRE
GROUND PLATES ARE TO BE INSTALLED TO A MINIMUM DEPTH OF 30-IN [76-CM]
GROUND PLATES SHALL BE MADE OF A COPPER ALLOY INTENDED FOR GROUNDING APPLICATIONS AND HAVE MINIMUM
DIMENSIONS AS FOLLOWS:
A.
FOR GROUNDING CONTROLLERS – 4-IN [10-CM] X 8-FT [1.2-M] X 0.0625-IN [1.5-MM] SOLID COPPER GROUNDING PLATE, A
25-FT [7.6-M] CONTINUOUS LENGTH OF 6 AWG, GREEN INSULATED, WITH EXTRUDED YELLOW STRIPE, SOLID BARE
COPPER WIRE WELDED TO THE PLATE (PAIGE ELECTRIC 182199IC) AND TWO 50-LB [22.6-KG] BAGS OF POWER SET EARTH
CONTACT MATERIAL OR TWO 50-LB [22.6-KG] BAGS OF POWERFILL EARTH CONTACT MATERIAL (PAIGE ELECTRIC 1820059)
FOR NON-POROUS SOILS
B.
FOR GROUNDING DECODERS – 4-IN [10-CM] X 3-FT [1-M] X 0.0625-IN [1.5-MM] SOLID COPPER GROUNDING PLATE, A 15-FT
[4.5-M] CONTINUOUS LENGTH OF 10 AWG, GREEN INSULATED, WITH EXTRUDED YELLOW STRIPE, SOLID BARE COPPER
WIRE IS WELDED TO THE PLATE (PAIGE ELECTRIC 182201IC) AND ONE 50-LB [22.6-KG] BAG OF POWER SET EARTH
CONTACT MATERIAL OR ONE 50-LB [22.6-KG] BAGS OF POWERFILL EARTH CONTACT MATERIAL (PAIGE ELECTRIC 1820059)
FOR NON-POROUS SOILS
FOR USE OF GROUNDING ROD:
GROUND ROD SHALL BE 5/8-IN [15-MM] DIAMETER X 8-FT [1.2-M] LONG COPPER CLAD STEEL GROUND RODS WITH 15-FT [4.5-M]
PRE-WELDED #6 AWG INSULATED GREEN-YELLOW WIRE (PAIGE ELECTRIC PART # 182000IC6)
GROUND ROD SHALL BE DRIVEN INTO THE GROUND IN A VERTICAL POSITION OR AN OBLIQUE ANGLE NOT TO EXCEED 45
DEGREES AT A LOCATION 10-FT [3-M] FROM THE ELECTRONIC EQUIPMENT, THE GROUND PLATE, OR THE WIRES AND CABLES
CONNECTED TO EQUIPMENT BEING GROUNDED
ADDITIONAL GROUND ROD IN DAISY CHAIN INSTALLATION SHALL BE 5/8-IN [15-MM] DIAMETER X 8-FT [1.2-M] LONG COPPER CLAD
STEEL GROUND RODS WITH 25-FT [4.5-M] PRE-WELDED #6 AWG INSULATED GREEN-YELLOW WIRE (PAIGE ELECTRIC PART
#182007IC6)
GROUND RODS SHALL BE COVERED BY A VALVE BOX
ALL CIRCUIT COMPONENTS SHALL BE INSTALLED IN STRAIGHT LINES
GROUND ROD AND PLATE LOCATION
CONTRACTOR SHALL LOCATE AND INSTALL GROUND ROD AND/OR PLATE IN AREA OF REGULAR MOIST SOIL TO MAXIMZE
ELECTRICAL CONDUCTIVITY
TWO-WIRE IRRIGATION NOTES

GENERAL PLAN 2040
The following policies of General Plan 2040 may be applicable to the project. 
Land Use Element
•
Mixed-Use Medium II (FAR:4.0, Density:51-99 du/ac, Max. Height: 5-8 stories): This 
designation allows medium-density mixed-use buildings that provide a mix of commercial, 
office, and/or residential uses within the same site or building. It is intended to allow a mix of 
uses near other mixed-use, commercial, or residential areas, and within Downtown. 
•
Mixed-Use High (FAR:4.5, Density: 100-130 du/ac, Max. Height: 4-6 stories): This designation 
allows high-density mixed-use buildings that provide a mix of commercial, office, and/or 
residential uses within the same site or building. It is intended to allow a mix of uses near major 
streets, train stations, and shopping centers, and within Downtown. 
•
Policy LU 1.4 - Mixed-Use. Encourage mixed-use developments to include increased residential 
components to provide greater proximity between jobs and housing, promote pedestrian 
activity, and reduce traffic congestion and vehicle miles traveled (“VMT”). 
•
Policy LU 2.2 - Caltrain Stations and El Camino Real Minimum Densities. Require new 
residential development within a half mile of a Caltrain station or within one block of the El 
Camino Real corridor to meet the minimum density established by the applied land use 
designation and encourage new development to achieve maximum density.
•
Policy LU 2.3 - Community Benefits. Develop a framework to allow density/intensity bonuses 
and concessions in exchange for the provision of community benefits, such as additional 
affordable housing, increased open space, public plazas or recreational facilities, subsidized 
retail space for small businesses, subsidized community space for nonprofits that provide 
community support services or childcare facilities, pedestrian and multimodal safety 
improvements, and/or off-site infrastructure improvements above minimum requirements. 
The framework shall allow for nonresidential development (office and commercial) within ¼-
mile of the Hayward Park and Hillsdale Caltrain stations to have heights up to eight-stories when 
commensurate community benefits are provided. 
•
Policy LU 3.1 - Housing Diversity. Promote safe, attractive, and walkable residential 
neighborhoods with diverse types and sizes of homes for individuals, families, and households of 
all income levels
•
Policy LU 3.5 - Support Service Uses. Encourage businesses that provide a variety of services, 
such as restaurants, child care facilities, medical clinics, gyms, pharmacies, hardware stores, and 
grocery stores in locations that serve residential neighborhoods and commercial/office uses. 
Prioritize the development of these services in equity priority communities in the city.
Comment: The plan does not include information to demonstrate the project provide service 
uses to the residential development, such as childcare facilities, medical clinics, and grocery 
stores. 
343 of 551

--- page 344 ---
•
Policy LU 3.9 - Workplaces. Develop office buildings and business parks to facilitate transit, 
pedestrian, and bicycle commutes. Provide compact development, mixed uses, and connectivity 
to transit to reduce vehicle miles traveled (VMT).
•
Policy LU 3.11 - Community Gathering Places. Provide and maintain inviting public spaces and 
streets that provide space for all members of the San Mateo community to meet, gather, and 
enjoy.
•
Policy LU 3.12 - Publicly Accessible Spaces. Integrate a variety of privately owned and 
maintained publicly accessible spaces into new development. Spaces should be safe, welcoming, 
easy to access, and include signage that clearly identifies these spaces as publicly accessible.
•
Policy LU 3.13 - Cultural Facilities and Public Art. Recognize cultural facilities, entertainment 
events, performing arts, and public art as part of a healthy and thriving community. Use funds 
from the City’s art in-lieu fee to enhance existing public art and cultural facilities and encourage 
new facilities that reflect the character and identity of the surrounding neighborhoods.
•
Policy LU 5.2 - El Camino Real Landscaping. Retain the general residential and landscaped 
character of El Camino Real north of Tilton Avenue. Promote the visual upgrading of El Camino 
Real south of 9th Avenue through increased landscaping, coordination of public improvements, 
property maintenance, and sign control, and through conformance with the El Camino Real 
Master Plan or a future consolidated Corridor Plan per Action LU 5-3.
•
Policy LU 6.1 - Rail Corridor Transit-Oriented Development Plan (Rail Corridor Plan). Continue 
to implement the Rail Corridor Plan to allow, encourage, and provide guidance for the creation 
of world-class transit-oriented, mixed-use development (TOD) within a half-mile radius of the 
Hillsdale and Hayward Park Caltrain stations, while maintaining and improving the quality of life 
for those who already live and work in the area.
•
Policy LU 6.2 - Hillsdale Shopping Center. Allow redevelopment of the Hillsdale Shopping Center 
for a mix of uses, including commercial, retail, office, hotel, and residential uses. Update the 
Hillsdale Station Area Plan or require preparation of a master development plan to ensure the 
site is developed comprehensively and provides appropriate transitions to the adjacent 
neighborhoods. 
Circulation Element
•
Policy C1.2 - Complete Streets. Apply complete streets design standards to future projects in 
the public right-of-way and on private property. Complete streets are streets designed to 
facilitate safe, comfortable, and efficient travel for all users regardless of age or ability or 
whether they are walking, bicycling, taking transit, or driving, and should include landscaping 
and shade trees as well as green streets stormwater infrastructure to reduce runoff and 
pollution.
•
Policy C1.4 - Prioritize Pedestrian and Bicycle Mobility Needs. Prioritize local pedestrian and 
bicycle projects that enhance mobility, connectivity, and safety when designing roadway and 
intersection improvements.
344 of 551

--- page 345 ---
•
Policy C1.9 - Dedication of Right-of-Way for Transportation Improvements. Require dedication 
of needed right-of-way for transportation improvements identified in adopted City plans, 
including pedestrian facilities, bikeways, and trails.
•
Action C2.5 - Facilitate TDM Services. Facilitate the provision of TDM services to employees and 
residents through development agreements, Transportation Management Associations, and 
coordination with regional partners.
Community Design and Historic Resources Element
•
Policy CD 3.2 - Replacement Planting. Require appropriate replacement planting or payment of 
an in-lieu fee when protected trees on public or private property are removed.
•
Policy CD 3.6 - New Development Street Trees. Require street tree planting where feasible as a 
condition of all new developments.
•
Policy CD 6.1 - New Development Street Trees. Require street tree planting where feasible as a 
condition of all new developments.
•
Policy CD 6.3 - Sustainable Design. Encourage integration of sustainable design features and 
elements into the design of new buildings, including locating and orienting buildings to access 
solar exposure, preserving mature vegetation to the extent feasible, and using green building 
materials.
•
Policy CD 6.6 - Signage. Maintain signage controls that appropriately regulate the design, size, 
type, illumination, and quantity of signs visible from corridors and create consistent signage that 
reinforces San Mateo’s unique identity.
•
Policy CD 6.7 - Public Open Space Design. Seek opportunities to establish public open spaces in 
new developments and new public buildings, and promote innovative and creative designs to 
create exceptional, unique, and functional spaces. Require signage that clearly delineates these 
spaces as publicly accessible.
•
Policy CD 6.8 - Public Art. Continue to require public art as part of new development and ensure 
the art is visible and accessible to the public. Support public art as a resource that enhances the 
quality of life for individuals living in, working in, and visiting the city, improves the quality of the 
urban environment, and increases property values.
•
Policy CD 6.9 - Inclusive Outreach. Involve the community in the City’s efforts to develop and 
maintain an attractive urban fabric that reflects San Mateo’s unique visual and architectural 
character. Use outreach and engagement methods that include broad representation and are 
culturally sensitive, particularly for equity priority communities. Communicate clearly how and 
at what stages members of the public can provide input for development projects under review.
•
Policy CD 7.3 - Multifamily Design. Encourage architectural design of new multifamily 
developments that enhances a neighborhood’s visual and architectural character by providing 
context sensitive building and pedestrian-scale elements, high-quality materials and 
construction, open space, and resident amenities.
345 of 551

--- page 346 ---
•
Policy CD 7.4 - Multifamily Parking. Require new multifamily developments to design and site 
parking to avoid blank, ground-floor walls and to screen views of parking from the street. 
•
Policy CD 7.5 - Multifamily Open Space. Require that a portion of required open space for new 
multifamily projects be useable for passive or active recreation. 
•
Policy CD 7.6 - Nighttime Lighting. Require nighttime lighting to be energy efficient and 
designed to minimize light pollution and light spillage on adjacent properties, while protecting 
public safety.
•
Policy CD 8.2 - Human-Scale Design. Cultivate pedestrian activity in commercial and mixed-use 
areas by providing adequate sidewalk widths, activating ground-floor street façades with active 
uses, windows, plantings, and awnings, using high-quality construction materials, and including 
human-scale details and architectural features.
•
Policy CD 8.3 - Respect Existing Scale and Rhythm. New mixed-use and commercial 
development should have context sensitive design that incorporates architectural styles and 
elements that relate to the scale and design of surrounding buildings, including by providing 
breaks in the building face at spacings common to buildings in the area and by stepping back 
upper floors.
•
Policy CD 8.4 - Commercial Parking. Encourage commercial projects to provide required parking 
underground to minimize the amount of ground-floor area dedicated to parking. When parking 
is at-grade, it should be located towards the rear of a parcel, away from active street frontages 
and public spaces.
Open Space Element
•
Policy COS 1.8 - Development Near Water or Wetlands – Avoid wetlands development where 
feasible (as defined under California Environmental Quality Act [CEQA] Guidelines, Section 
15364). Restrict or modify proposed development in areas that contain wetlands or waters to 
ensure the continued health and survival of special-status species and sensitive habitat areas. 
Development projects shall be designed to avoid impacts on sensitive resources, or to 
adequately mitigate impacts by providing on-site or off-site replacement at a higher ratio. 
Project design modification should include adequate avoidance measures, such as the use of 
setbacks, buffers, and water quality, drainage-control features, or other measures to ensure 
that no net loss of wetland acreage, function, water quality protection, and habitat value occurs. 
This may include the use of setbacks, buffers, and water quality, drainage control features, or 
other measures to maintain existing habitat and hydrologic functions of retained wetlands and 
waters of the US.” 
•
Policy COS 3.1 - Aesthetic and Habitat Values – Public Creeks. Preserve and enhance the 
aesthetic and habitat values of creeks, such as San Mateo, Laurel, and Beresford Creeks, and 
other City owned channels in all activities affecting these creeks, including revegetation, 
rewilding, erosion control, and adequate setbacks for structures.
•
Policy COS 4.7- Air Quality Construction Impacts. Require new construction and grading 
activities to mitigate air quality impacts generated during construction activities in compliance 
with BAAQMD’s regulations and guidelines on construction activity impacts.
346 of 551

--- page 347 ---
•
Policy COS 4.8 - Truck Facilities. Require new development, when applicable, to provide 
adequate truck parking loading space, and generators for refrigerated trucks to prevent idling 
during truck operation.
•
Policy COS 6.3 - Privately Owned Public Spaces. Require privately owned publicly accessible 
open space to be designed in a way that is welcoming for all, including public access signage and 
minimal physical or visual barriers, to ensure that the space is open and available to the 
community.
•
Policy COS 7.2 - Acreage Standards. Acquire or accept for dedication 2 acres of neighborhood 
and community parks per 1,000 residents. 
Public Services and Facilities Element
•
Policy PSF 2.4 - Water Supply for New Development. Require applicants to provide will-serve 
letters from water purveyors prior to issuing building permits for new development to 
demonstrate that water supply is available.
•
Policy PSF 2.6 - Water Offset Requirements. Require all new development or redevelopment 
projects to comply with the water conservation and offset policies and requirements imposed 
by California Water Service or Estero Municipal Improvement District, depending on the water 
service area in which the project is located.
•
Policy PSF 3.2 - Sewer Requirements for New Development. Require new multifamily and 
commercial developments to evaluate the main sewer lines in the project vicinity, which will be 
used by the new development and make any improvements necessary to convey the additional 
sewage flows.
•
Policy PSF 3.10 - New Creekside Development Requirements. Require that new creek side 
development protect and improve setbacks, banks, and waterways adjacent to the development 
projects to increase flood protection and enhance riparian vegetation and water quality. Prevent 
erosion of creek banks.
•
Policy PSF 4.10 - Private Utility Undergrounding. Require new private development to 
underground service connections onto private property.
•
Policy PSF 6.5 - Policy Child Care Centers in Residential and Employment Areas. Encourage 
child care centers in residential neighborhoods where they meet City standards and at 
employment centers.
Noise Element
•
Policy N 1.2 - Interior Noise Level Standard. Require submittal of an acoustical analysis and 
interior noise insulation for all noise-sensitive land uses listed in Table N-1 that have an exterior 
noise level of 60 dBA (Ldn ) or above, as shown on Figure N-2. The maximum interior noise level 
shall not exceed 45 dBA (Ldn ) in any habitable rooms, as established by the California Building 
Code.
347 of 551

--- page 348 ---
•
Policy N 1.3 - Exterior Noise Level Standard for Residential Uses. Require an acoustical analysis 
for new multifamily common open space for residents that have an exterior noise level of 60 
dBA (Ldn ) or above, as shown on Figure N-2. Incorporate necessary mitigation measures into 
residential project design to minimize common open space noise levels. Maximum exterior 
noise should not exceed 65 dBA (Ldn ) for residential uses.
•
Policy N 2.2 - Minimize Noise Impacts. Incorporate necessary mitigation measures into new 
development design to minimize short-term noise impacts. Determine whether new 
development has the potential to result in a significant noise impact on existing development 
based on the following standards. Impacts will be analyzed based on long-term operational 
noise increases at the sensitive receptor property line, or new uses that generate noise levels at 
the sensitive receptor property line, as follows:
•
Policy N 2.3 - Minimize Commercial Noise. Protect land uses other than those listed as “noise 
sensitive” in Table N-1 from adverse impacts caused by the on-site noise generated by new 
developments. Incorporate necessary mitigation measures into development design to minimize 
short-term and long-term noise impacts. Prohibit new uses that generate noise levels of 65 dBA 
(Ldn ) or above at the property line, excluding existing ambient noise levels.
•
Policy N 2.4 - Traffic Noise. Recognize projected increases in ambient noise levels resulting from 
future traffic increases, as shown on Figure N-2. Promote reduced traffic speeds and the 
installation of noise barriers or other methods to reduce traffic noise along highways and high-
volume roadways where noise-sensitive land uses (listed in Table N-1) are adversely impacted 
by excessive noise levels (60 dBA [Ldn ] or above).
•
Policy N 2.7 - Construction Noise and Vibration Monitoring. Require construction noise limits 
and vibration monitoring around sensitive receptors, including through limiting construction 
hours and individual and cumulative noise from construction equipment. For larger 
development projects that demand intensive construction periods and/or use equipment that 
could create vibration impacts, require a vibration impact analysis, as well as monitoring and 
reporting of noise/vibration levels throughout construction, consistent with industry standards.  
HILLSDALE STATION AREA PLAN 
Adopted in 2009, the Hillsdale Station Area Plan (HSAP) identifies the Hillsdale Mall remaining as the 
regional shopping center with potential housing development opportunities. The Area Plan envisions the 
addition of small retail storefronts along El Camino Real to enhance pedestrian activity and street-level 
engagement. Any major modifications to the Mall or surrounding site are anticipated to require a 
comprehensive master plan. Given the context in which the Area Plan was established, the master plan 
process is expected to be discretionary and implemented through legislative action at that time. 
Although HSAP identifies very limited improvement is needed to implement HSAP, the water supply 
assessment for HSAP does not include redevelopment capacity proposed in this application. The 
required fire flow for a particular development will most likely dictate whether upgrades to the existing 
water lines will need to be made. Therefore, water supply assessment is required for this application.
 Below are applicable policies. 
348 of 551

--- page 349 ---
•
Setbacks – Buildings shall be set back from El Camino Real to create a 10-foot effective sidewalk 
wide enough for a pleasant pedestrian environment. This shall be established per the 
requirements of the City’s Zoning Code and shall be consistently applied throughout the Station 
Area. (Page 69 of HSAP)
•
Buildings shall be set back from El Camino Real consistent with the requirements of City’s Zoning 
Code and the El Camino Real Master Plan, in order to provide for a 10-foot effective sidewalk 
width, wide enough for a pleasant pedestrian environment. (Page 72 of HSAP)
-
Buildings should be built to this effective sidewalk setback. 
-
Buildings are strongly encouraged to have portions set back to create usable outdoor space. 
Planters and well-designed, low-sitting fences should be used to define the edge of the 
outdoor space. 
•
Stepbacks - Buildings are strongly encouraged to provide additional setback to create urban 
open spaces. These should be consistent at the four corners of an intersection; would remain 
part of private development; and would not be publicly dedicated (Page 78 of HSAP): 
-
El Camino Real: 30 feet beyond that described in Section B; 10 feet beyond for buildings that 
are two stories and/or 28 feet in height or less. 
-
East-West Avenues: 20 feet beyond that described in Section C; 10 feet beyond for buildings 
that are two stories and/or 28 feet in height or less. 
•
As an alternative to open space setbacks, buildings located at key intersections shall be oriented 
and architecturally designed to emphasize the corner as a node of activity and architectural 
prominence. Solutions for developing projects that are of an exemplary quality include (Page 79 
of HSAP):
-
Tower elements as a prominent massing feature 
-
Entry plazas on corner sites 
-
Fountains or water features 
-
Distinct changes in the building volume at the primary entry 
-
Prominent landscape features, such as tall trees 
-
Dramatic building lighting for nighttime effect 
-
Public art installations 
The primary building entry should be oriented towards the corner and be visible from the 
intersection. 
•
Massing Stepbacks (Page 70 of HSAP):
-
Buildings taller than three stories are strongly encouraged to step back at least 6 feet above 
the third floor. 
-
Within that stepback, balconies are permitted and encouraged. 
-
Stepbacks are not required, and are strongly discouraged, for the portions of the building 
that face any open space developed at key intersections. 
•
New development shall limit the number of new curb cuts onto El Camino Real, including 
shared access where feasible, side street access, and use of existing curb cuts.

--- page 350 ---
•
Frontage (El Camino Real) (Page 69 of HSAP):
-
Ground floors of buildings within 100 feet of and fronting on El Camino Real shall include 
building transparency of at least 50% of the building’s street frontage and shall include the 
primary building entrance. Properties on the west side of El Camino Real that are part of the 
Hillsdale Shopping Center may include store display windows in calculating 50% 
transparency and are encouraged to have secondary entrances along El Camino Real. Where 
residential uses are allowed on El Camino Real, they are exempt from this guideline. (Page 
70 of HSAP):
-
El Camino Real street frontage should include primary building entrances. 
-
For the Hillsdale Shopping Center site, transparency requirement can be satisfied with 
display windows. Secondary entrances are “encouraged.” 
-
North of 31st Avenue, require non-residential ground-floor uses in the Active Zone of the 
Station Area, defined as the portion of parcels that face onto El Camino Real from 25th to 
31st Avenues and the portion of parcels that face onto 25th Avenue. This requirement 
applies only to the first 30 feet of depth of a building facing onto El Camino Real. For parcels 
with more than 300 feet of frontage along El Camino Real, a minimum of 50% of the parcel 
frontage (measured in linear feet) must meet this requirement. Residential entryways, 
lobbies, and other accessory uses related to upper story residential are permitted. (Page 51 
of HSAP):
-
Residential buildings on El Camino Real are exempt from the HSAP requirements. 
-
In no case shall blank walls be permitted on buildings facing El Camino Real. (Page 69 of 
HSAP):
•
Laurel Creek Guidelines & Standards (page 79-80 of HSAP).
-
Buildings shall be set back from Laurel Creek consistent with the City’s General Plan and 
zoning regulations. 
-
This setback should be designed as a passive park-like setting, which could include trails, and 
be publicly accessible. 
-
No solid fencing should be installed along the creek. This will ensure an open and safe 
environment. If fencing is required, the fence should be designed with visibility in mind, 
using high-quality materials, and be a maximum of 4 feet in height. 
-
Development should orient windows and entries to face the creek to provide “natural 
surveillance” on the creek throughout the day. 
-
In order to reinforce the identity of the creek, a monument sign highlighting the presence of 
Laurel Creek should be erected in a location that is clearly visible to pedestrians. 
-
The sign should not be so large or placed in a location that presents a visual distraction or 
obstruction for residents, pedestrians, or drivers. 
•
Pedestrian Paseos (El Camino Real) (page 70-80 of HSAP)
-
Mixed-use and residential development on parcels more than 300 feet deep on the east side 
of El Camino Real must provide a north-west pedestrian path at least 20 feet wide. The 
pathway shall have lighting consistent with pedestrian-scale lighting proposed on El Camino 
Real, and include pedestrian amenities similar to those found on public sidewalks. 
-
Pedestrian paseos are required for “[m]ixed-use and residential development on parcels 
more than 300 feet deep on the east side of El Camino Real”
